  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_cfc31618-5edd-4ea3-b413-50fe2e6167e4'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer8710537172454076271">The groundbreaking, bestselling classic, now available in a special fortieth-anniversary edition that includes a new Foreword from Eben Alexander, M.D., author of Proof of Heaven, and a new Afterword by the author.<br/><br/>Raymond Moody is the “father” of the modern NDE (Near Death Experience) movement, and his pioneering work Life After Life transformed the world, revolutionizing </span>
  <span id="freeText8710537172454076271" style="display:none">The groundbreaking, bestselling classic, now available in a special fortieth-anniversary edition that includes a new Foreword from Eben Alexander, M.D., author of Proof of Heaven, and a new Afterword by the author.<br /><br />Raymond Moody is the “father” of the modern NDE (Near Death Experience) movement, and his pioneering work Life After Life transformed the world, revolutionizing the way we think about death and what lies beyond. Originally published in 1975, it is the groundbreaking study of one hundred people who experienced “clinical death” and were revived, and who tell, in their own words, what lies beyond death.<br /><br />A smash bestseller that has sold more than thirteen million copies around the globe, Life After Life introduced us to concepts—including the bright light, the tunnel, the presence of loved ones waiting on the other side—that have become cultural memes today, and paved the way for modern bestsellers by Eben Alexander, Todd Burpo, Mary Neal, and Betty Eadie that have shaped countless readers notions about the end life and the meaning of death.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8710537172454076271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16797755524326064124">I had just started my first work, I was going to continue a phD and start my own business and then it hit me, we're all going to die.<br/><br/>I was plundering into a state of paramount depression, I found out what I was experiencing was called an existential crisis and after a week of staying at home sleeping I decided to seek truth, I prayed more sincerely than I have ever done, I prayed God (which I was questioning his existence) helps me understand and then somehow instantaneously I stumbled upon this</span>
  <span id="freeText16797755524326064124" style="display:none">I had just started my first work, I was going to continue a phD and start my own business and then it hit me, we're all going to die.<br /><br />I was plundering into a state of paramount depression, I found out what I was experiencing was called an existential crisis and after a week of staying at home sleeping I decided to seek truth, I prayed more sincerely than I have ever done, I prayed God (which I was questioning his existence) helps me understand and then somehow instantaneously I stumbled upon this book.<br /><br />I figured out there are things beyond human understanding and there are phenomena you can't explain, the signs are there you just have to search, knock and the doors will open, ask and you will be answered, but whatever you do weather you're an atheist or devoutly religious, LOVE! not just your wife/husband or girlfriend/boyfriend, love your friends your neighbours your family...In short love humanity because this is the true meaning of this life and the one after, God exists because love exists.</span>

<div id="review_179047106" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/179047106" />
    <a title="Tara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2749604-tara"><img alt="Tara" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/179047106?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tara" href="/user/show/2749604-tara">Tara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer179047106" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13857656268225713969">This is my first book that I've read about people's life after death experiences. I knew that many people had such experiences and so I looked on amazon to see if any books had been written. I was surprised to see just how many books have been written. I chose to read Life after Life because it "investigates more than one hundred case studies of people who experienced "clinical death" and were subsequently revived," and then categorizes these people's experiences into events that the people expe</span>
  <span id="freeText13857656268225713969" style="display:none">This is my first book that I've read about people's life after death experiences. I knew that many people had such experiences and so I looked on amazon to see if any books had been written. I was surprised to see just how many books have been written. I chose to read Life after Life because it "investigates more than one hundred case studies of people who experienced "clinical death" and were subsequently revived," and then categorizes these people's experiences into events that the people experienced in common. I was pleasantly surprised to see that most people experience very similar events, no matter what their background. I especially enjoyed reading about "the personage of light" that many people encounter and the feeling of love that they feel in this person's presence. Although I've always had hope and faith in life after death, this book has increased that conviction and has taken away any fear of death that resided within my darker corners. Although the author is a professor at the University of Nevada, which should say something about his credibility, unfortunately, at the end of the book he wrote about things that lessened his credibility in my mind, such as that he has developed techniques for people to contact the dead and visit the other side, etc. I don't believe that such things can occur by man's will, only by God's. Nevertheless, I still think the book is worth reading. I look forward to comparing this to other books on life after death.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13857656268225713969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_656339530" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/656339530" />
    <a title="Nancy Rossman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4086737-nancy-rossman"><img alt="Nancy Rossman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442518876p2/4086737.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/656339530?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy Rossman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy Rossman" href="/user/show/4086737-nancy-rossman">Nancy Rossman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer656339530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7193921307815532242">Nothing, NOTHING has our fascination or questions more than death. DEAD? life afterward? not to mention all the various religious interpretations. <br/><br/>There had been too many patients that confidentially reported their own remembrances of NDE (near death experience). A flow through a tunnel or tube, dark but not scary, warm, floating, and more. He decided to interview, as it turned out, 150 people and see if their were common elements in what they "saw" and remembered.<br/><br/>Dr. Moody's own reluctance but </span>
  <span id="freeText7193921307815532242" style="display:none">Nothing, NOTHING has our fascination or questions more than death. DEAD? life afterward? not to mention all the various religious interpretations. <br /><br />There had been too many patients that confidentially reported their own remembrances of NDE (near death experience). A flow through a tunnel or tube, dark but not scary, warm, floating, and more. He decided to interview, as it turned out, 150 people and see if their were common elements in what they "saw" and remembered.<br /><br />Dr. Moody's own reluctance but desire to investigate gave him enough legitimate standing to find out just what people were saying. Where they thought they "went" and what they saw. Enough detail and verification is/was added that the person who had the experience couldn't have possibly known if what they said hadn't happened.<br /><br />And this is book is not just a diatribe of a single instance that has made some people wealthy for the book deal (Heaven can Wait, Dying to be Me, are two good examples) but rather this is a selected group of as I said, 150, with detailed accounts of what happened (anonymous only because those who volunteered didn't want scrutiny or fame). <br /><br />It's quite food for thought, to borrow a much maligned cliché. And a quick read. If you are with aging loved ones who are afraid, or if you are curious but scared yourself this could be valuable. We are, as you know, all dying. That is for sure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7193921307815532242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1409553538" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1409553538" />

<span id="freeTextContainer5537293158842269701">A doctor in search of an answer to the age old question - Is there life after death? - interviews numerous people whom have died and been brought back. <br/><br/>I, personally, will be forever thankful to the nurse who refused to give up on my Momma 45 years ago, while the doctor was telling my Dad that he was sorry and they did all they could to save her, the nurse (a family friend) had stayed in the room, climbed up on the bed, straddled Momma's waist, hooked her hands together and brought them down on </span>
  <span id="freeText5537293158842269701" style="display:none">A doctor in search of an answer to the age old question - Is there life after death? - interviews numerous people whom have died and been brought back. <br /><br />I, personally, will be forever thankful to the nurse who refused to give up on my Momma 45 years ago, while the doctor was telling my Dad that he was sorry and they did all they could to save her, the nurse (a family friend) had stayed in the room, climbed up on the bed, straddled Momma's waist, hooked her hands together and brought them down on Momma's chest with "everything in me". The paddles hadn't worked but the sheer determination and love of this little nurse started her heart and brought Momma back.<br />Of course, Momma was furious because she said "I was in Heaven, why didn't ya'll just leave me alone."<br />Ah, Momma, you're there now and I miss you ... every minute of every day.</span>

<div id="review_319923740" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/319923740" />
    <a title="Marguerite Harden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9040688-marguerite-harden"><img alt="Marguerite Harden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351288614p2/9040688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/319923740?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marguerite Harden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marguerite Harden" href="/user/show/9040688-marguerite-harden">Marguerite Harden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer319923740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4473272345714781421">Raymond Moody-- a doctor and someone who has never had a near-death experience himself-- presents an unbiased account of years of case studies regarding trends behind what happens to some individuals after clinical death, and resuscitation thereafter. Personally, I have a science background combined with a strong faith, and this book does a great job of revealing a, "middle way of interpreting -- a way which neither rejects these experiences on the basis that they do not constitute scientific or</span>
  <span id="freeText4473272345714781421" style="display:none">Raymond Moody-- a doctor and someone who has never had a near-death experience himself-- presents an unbiased account of years of case studies regarding trends behind what happens to some individuals after clinical death, and resuscitation thereafter. Personally, I have a science background combined with a strong faith, and this book does a great job of revealing a, "middle way of interpreting -- a way which neither rejects these experiences on the basis that they do not constitute scientific or local proof NOR sensationalizes them by resorting to vague emotional claims that they 'prove' that there is life after death" (p. 163). <br /><br />After reading this book, I have found relief and comfort in the shared experiences of death, which are described in Chapter 2. In addition, I particularly enjoyed Chapter 3, which relates the personal case studies that had been relayed to Dr. Moody to historical texts, including mainstream religions (The Bible), philosophies (Plato), and even the Tibetan Book of the Dead.<br /><br />This book offers a historical, and insightful relation of some modern ideas relating to death and the potential for life after death. Because this book is the first notable book about near-death experiences, there is much defense of the research that was conducted, and the questions and skepticism that arise from these conversations are well vetted. I appreciated these sections, but I'm also looking forward to reading more books on the subject that speak are aimed more at the believers than the skeptics.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to people of all types, including those with spiritual or religious backgrounds, and those without; those with an open mind to what happens near and after death, and especially to those who are skeptical of the idea that anything happens after death. I appreciate this dialogue and wish the topic of death was a less taboo topic in our society, as Dr. Moody points out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4473272345714781421" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_473702006" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/473702006" />
    <a title="Mark Maguire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8027717-mark-maguire"><img alt="Mark Maguire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1331936648p2/8027717.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/473702006?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark Maguire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark Maguire" href="/user/show/8027717-mark-maguire">Mark Maguire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8027717-mark-maguire?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8027717-mark-maguire?shelf=psychology">psychology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8027717-mark-maguire?shelf=popular-culture">popular-culture</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer473702006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer807165569773421839">This was a challenging, and thought-provoking read, which posed as many questions as it attempted to answer. <br/><br/><br/>The primary reason for reading this book was to try and find an answer to the following question: "can human consciousness survive bodily death"? I have been asking this question for a number of years, and I have approached a number of authority figues in relation to this question, and I all have ever received has been either obfuscation, or a guarded "yes", dependent upon one's conduct i</span>
  <span id="freeText807165569773421839" style="display:none">This was a challenging, and thought-provoking read, which posed as many questions as it attempted to answer. <br /><br /><br />The primary reason for reading this book was to try and find an answer to the following question: "can human consciousness survive bodily death"? I have been asking this question for a number of years, and I have approached a number of authority figues in relation to this question, and I all have ever received has been either obfuscation, or a guarded "yes", dependent upon one's conduct in the present-life. <br /><br /><br />It would seem to be a remarkable, and almost inexplicable feat for consciousness to survive bodily death, but having read the cases contained within the book, the almost formulaic repsonses given by those whom have either died, or have come close to death, does make for startling reading, and has brought me a step closer to a considered answer to the question above. <br /><br /><br />The key problem that the Author runs into is the problem of "proof". At the time of writing, it has not proven possible to provide evidence of the existence of an afterlife within the socially-accepted boundaries of modern science. The current inability to quantify the afterlife, means, in the majority of cases, that studies in this field are dubbed "pseudo-scientific" or as being simply delusional. <br /><br />The Author does try to answer a number of questions that have been raised over the years since the book's original publication, and also evidences a number of comparisons between drug-induced hallucinations; dreams, and out of body experiences, all of which seek to challenge the orthodoxy that the subjects involved can be explained either medically or by reference to religious faith. However, within the accepted norms of the day, we have no definitive proof of an Afterlife. The question and answer session does go some way to pointing to an academic rigour which is missing from most other works within the field. <br /><br /><br />The highlight of the book surprisingly, resides not within the incredible personal accounts of the Afterlife, but within the chapter on psychological explanations for the aforementioned experiences, which is one of the most rigorous and thought-provoking chapters that I have read thus far. Having recently read Koestler, I certainly feel that any "proof" of the existence of the Afterlife resides within the critical distinction between the Brain and the Mind,and thus our understanding of the Ghost in the Machine. <br /><br /><br />This was a fascinating read, and I certainly feel that I making progress with my professed aim of answering the question: "can consciousness survive bodily death". <br /><br /><br /> <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="807165569773421839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_709748521" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/709748521" />
    <a title="Lisa Temple" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14492458-lisa-temple"><img alt="Lisa Temple" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374439144p2/14492458.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/709748521?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Temple" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Temple" href="/user/show/14492458-lisa-temple">Lisa Temple</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone interested in the subject</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lisa by: </span>
      I watched a documentary on it
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer709748521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10154283682160805301">LIfe After Life, written by fellow Alabamian, Paul Moody, covers a subject that I have long found compelling - "near death experiences." You know, those strange occurrences when a person who is clinically "dead," actually sees him or herself from a vantage point way above their lifeless body. Many times they also experience the sensation of "going toward the light." We all know to call these type of happenings, "near death experiences," because Dr. Moody told us to - he coined the phrase.<br/><br/>Part of</span>
  <span id="freeText10154283682160805301" style="display:none">LIfe After Life, written by fellow Alabamian, Paul Moody, covers a subject that I have long found compelling - "near death experiences." You know, those strange occurrences when a person who is clinically "dead," actually sees him or herself from a vantage point way above their lifeless body. Many times they also experience the sensation of "going toward the light." We all know to call these type of happenings, "near death experiences," because Dr. Moody told us to - he coined the phrase.<br /><br />Part of me thinks the whole phenomenon is like mediums - too good to be true. But, Dr. Moody seems an up-and-up kind of guy, and he has spoken to thousands of folks who all have had roughly the same experience. Those interviews are documented in "Life After Life: The Investigation of a Phenomenon - Survival of Bodily Death," as well as quite a few other books written by Dr. Moody alone and with other contributors.<br /><br />The only reason why I didn't give the book 5 stars is because it was a little more "clinical" than what I would like for it to have been. Call me lazy, but I just wanted to read a lot of "ghostly" stories and, perhaps, make myself feel a little better about the whole dying business. Don't get me wrong - there was plenty of that in the book - but, and I imagine this is necessary in order for Dr. Moody to come across as credible, there was also a great deal of documentation and back story, as well. I'm not sure if any of Dr. Moody's books satisfy my craving for back-to-back stories of "life after life." But I'll probably buy a few more of his books because the subject is fascinating and he is, hands down, the most expert in the field.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10154283682160805301" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1931727226" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1931727226" />
    <a title="Ken Oder" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22944208-ken-oder"><img alt="Ken Oder" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442975385p2/22944208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1931727226?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ken Oder" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ken Oder" href="/user/show/22944208-ken-oder">Ken Oder</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1931727226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4795757987461207356">As an undergraduate majoring in philosophy, Raymond Moody, attended a meeting in 1965 with Dr. George Ritchie, who spoke about his experience of being pronounced dead twice due to pneumonia in an Army hospital in 1943. Ritchie claimed his consciousness survived and traveled out of his body during more than nine minutes when he was clinically dead. Ritchie's presentation and demeanor had a profound effect on Moody. I can relate to this since I attended the same meeting and came away with the firm</span>
  <span id="freeText4795757987461207356" style="display:none">As an undergraduate majoring in philosophy, Raymond Moody, attended a meeting in 1965 with Dr. George Ritchie, who spoke about his experience of being pronounced dead twice due to pneumonia in an Army hospital in 1943. Ritchie claimed his consciousness survived and traveled out of his body during more than nine minutes when he was clinically dead. Ritchie's presentation and demeanor had a profound effect on Moody. I can relate to this since I attended the same meeting and came away with the firm conviction that Ritchie was sincere and truthful in what he believed happened to him. <br />Moody was so inspired that he spent the next forty-five years studying what he called "near death experiences" (NDE). During and after attaining a Ph.D. and M.D., he interviewed hundreds of people who survived NDE's. Where possible, he checked their medical records and related corroborating and invalidating data. He noticed striking similarities in their stories and came away convinced of the existence of an afterlife, but he doesn't force this conclusion on the reader. This book does not purport to be a clinical scientific study. It merely summarizes the interviews anecdotally and sets forth Moody's observations and conclusions. A flaw in the book in my view is that it gives short shrift to possible natural explanations for these phenomena, but it is otherwise a fascinating read. Originally published in 1975, the book helped launch the spirited debate and analysis about NDE's that continues today. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4795757987461207356" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

A lot of people experience a dark tunnel, a strange noise, being out of your body, and seeing yourself, and hearing exactly what is going on to your physical body. A lot of people exper</span>
  <span id="freeText18212099355238873884" style="display:none">The book life after life, is a book that shows life after a physical death. Throughout the book, different occurrences happen to different people. Some with very close or almost exact, identical descriptions about what personal experiences these people had between the time of death of when they come back to life. A lot of people experience a dark tunnel, a strange noise, being out of your body, and seeing yourself, and hearing exactly what is going on to your physical body. A lot of people experience a very quiet and peaceful feeling, and others meet other people, like family members or people who are close to you that have already died there to comfort you, they also see a very fast sort of playback of their life, and are sort of asked if they have accomplished a fulfilled life. People talked about a being of light, that was so comforting and filled with so much compassion, religious people believe this must have been God, or Jesus. This book also talks about the Bible, and the philosopher Plato teachings about life after life. I really enjoyed this book, because I think we are all curious about what happens after physical life. There is also a lot of debate and different beliefs about what happens after life, and here are the researched phenomenons of people who have experienced life after death, and I rate this book a 5 star, and I encourage everyone to read it!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1133227031339825353">Fascinating early work by Dr. Raymond Moody on the near death experiences (NDEs) of patients. Much of the proliferation of western NDE literature has its roots in Dr. Moody’s studies, which put it on my list of to-reads. Through a significant number of case studies, he recites the patient’s experience and then draws inferences of commonality between each that are compelling and bear further research.<br/><br/>Interesting material for knowledge-seekers and anyone interested in NDE or post-life studies.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_329567434" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/329567434" />
    <a title="Joseph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6553367-joseph"><img alt="Joseph" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/329567434?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joseph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joseph" href="/user/show/6553367-joseph">Joseph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780811709460" href="/book/show/2595014-life-after-life">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6553367-joseph?shelf=other">other</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer329567434" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9951171203780633937">Although this book goes against what I believe in some ways, and has not convinced me otherwise, it is still an interesting read, and given the increasing interest in near-death experiences, familiarity with this influential and easy-to-read study can be very enriching. <br/><br/>For what this book is, an explanation of the findings from a study regarding people's near death experiences, it isn't bad. It is very readable and approachable. It presents Moody's findings clearly with sufficient excerpts from </span>
  <span id="freeText9951171203780633937" style="display:none">Although this book goes against what I believe in some ways, and has not convinced me otherwise, it is still an interesting read, and given the increasing interest in near-death experiences, familiarity with this influential and easy-to-read study can be very enriching. <br /><br />For what this book is, an explanation of the findings from a study regarding people's near death experiences, it isn't bad. It is very readable and approachable. It presents Moody's findings clearly with sufficient excerpts from his actual interviews. It is not a huge sample (only about 150, if I recall correctly), but it is large enough to be relevant<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Now, I am a devout Christian, so obviously a number of the things these people claim to have experienced I don't believe actually happen. It is not my belief that most (i.e. pretty much everyone except those who commit suicide) go to a wonderful place of joy and peace regardless of their faith or lack of it in Jesus Christ. Nevertheless, for what this book is, it is pretty good. <br /><br />Also, as a Christian conditionalist (one who believes Hell is where the wicked are destroyed, not tortured for eternity), this kind of study is especially useful to me. Moody's conclusions, that people all survive physical death, obviously isn't consistent with the view that some will not live on forever after death (but are rather resurrected to be destroyed by God). However, this study, along with any number of other studies on people's near death experiences, fly in the face of those who claim to have had near death experiences and gone to "Hell", seen as a place of eternally unending fiery torture. If we should take a handful of these Hell experiences seriously, what about the over 100 people who almost all claim a joyous afterlife, regardless of religion or quality of life live? What about the numerous studies from before and after this one, all looking to thousands of people, the vast majority of whom not only claim a pleasant afterlife, but who all claim very similar experiences? If we are going to down this road, then there may be reason to believe that everyone essentially goes to a "heaven" as it were (though those who take their own lives are punished for a time, it seems) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There certainly isn't enough to convince anyone that the afterlife Moody's subjects claim to have seen is an accurate reflection of the truth. If one has a reason to believe differently (as I do), there's nothing compelling enough to seriously challenge you view. However, it is a very thought provoking book, and at the time, it was a pretty influential study. A number have criticized its many cliche's (bathing white light, seeing dead relatives, etc.), but keep in mind that this book is almost 40-years old, and preceded many studies that have made these things "cliche." It's an interesting read, and it ishelpful for people of any religious belief who have an interest in the differing views of the afterlife to be familiar with these types of empirical studies. This book is a great place to start.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9951171203780633937" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_74003340" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/74003340" />
    <a title="ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/712626-ann"><img alt="ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1227394762p2/712626.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/74003340?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ann" href="/user/show/712626-ann">ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer74003340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13793405397117613258">You've probably heard the cliché used that someone dies and reaches a light at the end of the tunnel. If you haven't heard it, you've seen it reenacted somewhere in a television sequence. If you like the movie "Ghost" you will probably find this an interesting read. This book was orginally published in 1975 and I'm guessing this is the text that gave this cliché cultural currency. <br/>That said, it is more than the fleshing out a cultural legend...it is group of case studies of people who have been </span>
  <span id="freeText13793405397117613258" style="display:none">You've probably heard the cliché used that someone dies and reaches a light at the end of the tunnel. If you haven't heard it, you've seen it reenacted somewhere in a television sequence. If you like the movie "Ghost" you will probably find this an interesting read. This book was orginally published in 1975 and I'm guessing this is the text that gave this cliché cultural currency. <br />That said, it is more than the fleshing out a cultural legend...it is group of case studies of people who have been clinically "dead" and then resuscitated. Dr. Moody presents them and notes the strong similarities, and repeating aspects of all the cases he heard. He makes no conclusions about "life" beyond death, but only presents the cases and invites others to build on his work.<br /><br />Three things I like very much about Dr. Moody as an author. First off, he allots a good portion of his book to pure testimonials. I would guess a third to a half of the book is witness accounting of what happened to them when they died. The second thing I admire about Moody is that he goes to great lengths to disclose and answer all skeptical questions. He does not claim this book is pure "research" or a "scientific study" but he uses his survey of cases as a basis for an abstract model of the first stages of death. I am guessing this is whatpsychiatrist researchers do when presented with an unknown behavior...I liked the approach...What is so fascinating is that the model can exist at all, because these cases do have similar traits.<br />Thirdly, as philosopher, he is able to relate these experiences to various cultural texts and religions...some of which closely corroborate his "model of symptons." I appreciate that the book is not purely clinical.<br /><br />This book won't necessarily change your life, but it may make you question certain abstracts in the living world...for instance why Christianity insists on a dichotomy of heaven and hell when none on these witnesses could really describe what they saw as either (or what they expected of either place.) On the flip side, many of the stories suggest that religion or some sort of spiritual practice is necessary and important for a person's development over a life. All of them suggest that we experience earthly reality in a limited, indirect, and discontinuous fashion that ends upon our death. Maybe you will find this comforting.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13793405397117613258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer3522989017802481073">Experts? What in tarnation makes these folks expert if they ain't been dead, huh? I been on over to the other side--dead, that is. I saw my collsarn body from the ceiling of the operatin' room and looked down at the docs tryin' to revive me, and the bleep, bleep, bleep of the monitor let out a high pitched beep of finality when I was called kablooey, kaput and flatlined finito.   <span id="freeText3522989017802481073" style="display:none">Experts? What in tarnation makes these folks expert if they ain't been dead, huh? I been on over to the other side--dead, that is. I saw my collsarn body from the ceiling of the operatin' room and looked down at the docs tryin' to revive me, and the bleep, bleep, bleep of the monitor let out a high pitched beep of finality when I was called kablooey, kaput and flatlined finito. I was plum done dead. That's right "Authorities" on the Survival of Bodily Death. Hell's fire, I done been there. I did not see the bright white light, no siree I saw a blurry red glob turned out bein'a tunnel that took me straight on to Hades! That's a fact, and I even been interviewed by docs of world renown. This ain't a topic lots of folks care to hear about no way because people want to believe, need to believe there's butterflies and unicorns, happy smiley face relatives, and everything is just la-ti-dah -- Guess what? It doesn't always go down that way. They kept my body on a ventilator so UNOS could harvest organs, and there I was floatin' around from chamber to chamber of the Devil's domain. Heaven? Please, that's the story folks want to hear, but fact is, hell's as real as my fingertips tappin' this keypad. I get the heebie-jeebies, jim-jams, and fantods thinkin' about it, but word's gotta get out. Go on read the accounts of my trip to Hades, how I escaped, and detail every bit of what you can look forward to in that crummy hellacious hereafter that's all hushed up. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13641192.Back_to_Hades_Eustice_Seeney_Returns_to_Hell" title="Back to Hades Eustice Seeney Returns to Hell by D.D. Cross" rel="nofollow noopener">Back to Hades: Eustice Seeney Returns to Hell</a>I've also been to heaven and as a matter of fact, it ain't all it's cut out to be. Thanks to some flukes of physics, neuro-chemical fandango, and a whole lot of other stuff, I seen heaven, and know what could be in store. So there. Read this: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17331888.Forheavenstake" title="Forheavenstake by D.D. Cross" rel="nofollow noopener">Forheavenstake</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3522989017802481073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14467530698851362196">Moody's classic, Life After Life, is a must read for all who have yet to be introduced to the near-death phenomenon. A large portion of this book is personal accounts of those who have experienced the survival of consciousness. In the second half of the book, possible explanations and religious/spiritual parallels are explored, but in the end, the subject is left open for the reader to consider. Many years have passed since this book was written and we still have no definite proof of life after </span>
  <span id="freeText14467530698851362196" style="display:none">Moody's classic, Life After Life, is a must read for all who have yet to be introduced to the near-death phenomenon. A large portion of this book is personal accounts of those who have experienced the survival of consciousness. In the second half of the book, possible explanations and religious/spiritual parallels are explored, but in the end, the subject is left open for the reader to consider. Many years have passed since this book was written and we still have no definite proof of life after death. However, we are closer than ever before to understanding the complexities of the human mind and science can still not explain these happenings fully. </span>

<div id="review_3396150563" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3396150563" />
    <a title="Muhammed Nijim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11476102-muhammed-nijim"><img alt="Muhammed Nijim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460638379p2/11476102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3396150563?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Muhammed Nijim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Muhammed Nijim" href="/user/show/11476102-muhammed-nijim">Muhammed Nijim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3396150563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14248194928903145896">A good read by Moody. As a believer in life after death, truths in this book were no surprise but an endorsement to what God says in the holy book of the Quran. The core value of this book though was the descriptions of the soul and some of its characteristics. A lot of people ignore many facts about the soul, which would change their life entirely if they just thought about it - the convergence of flesh and metaphysics in the human body. <br/><br/>According to Islam, the soul is granted by God, it is imm</span>
  <span id="freeText14248194928903145896" style="display:none">A good read by Moody. As a believer in life after death, truths in this book were no surprise but an endorsement to what God says in the holy book of the Quran. The core value of this book though was the descriptions of the soul and some of its characteristics. A lot of people ignore many facts about the soul, which would change their life entirely if they just thought about it - the convergence of flesh and metaphysics in the human body. <br /><br />According to Islam, the soul is granted by God, it is immortal; never dies. As confirmed by Moody, death is a transition from one life to another by leaving the material body and departing with the soul to start an entirely different life that we still know nothing about. I am saying we almost know nothing about because when one thinks about the experience of Moody, one would ask "did not God know about those people who would die but then come back to life?" <br /><br />Therefore, I am still worried and concerned about the uncertainty of death because this experience does not tell anything about life after death. According to Islam, there is a wall between life and death, and once one's soul transcends this wall that is called "Barzakh" or a divider that separates life from death, there would be no comeback. Based on my beliefs, the souls of these people that were interviewed by Moody were still hovering before the actual wall of death. One can explain what indeed happens after death when transcending that divider only, and given that nobody can do so, it is impossible to tell what happens when one dies, other than what is mentioned in some scriptures. <br /><br />Death is still a perplexing issue, it is the bitter truth of this life that puts an end to the mightiest of humans.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14248194928903145896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SrUaq1x5j1mhk9a65dNZTa/i/3OpCHKtplyX2fddskF0vU8cuMHNQRCAkF53ow2QDip0IzALI1F+Na+PBcPdGA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

As a scientist, this was difficult for him to accept: Wouldn\'t it be scientifically irresponsibl<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText17343700688949548358\" style=\"display:none\">As a cardiologist, Pim van Lommel was struck by the number of his patients who claimed to have near-death experiences as a result of their heart attacks. As a scientist, this was difficult for him to accept: Wouldn\'t it be scientifically irresponsible of him to ignore the evidence of these stories? Faced with this dilemma, van Lommel decided to design a research study to investigate the phenomenon under the controlled environment of a cluster of hospitals with a medically trained staff.\n\nFor more than twenty years van Lommel systematically studied such near-death experiences in a wide variety of hospital patients who survived a cardiac arrest. In 2001, he and his fellow researchers published his study on near-death experiences in the renowned medical journal The Lancet. The article caused an international sensation as it was the first scientifically rigorous study of this phenomenon. Now available for the first time in English, van Lommel offers an in-depth presentation of his results and theories in this book that has already sold over 125,000 copies in Europe.\n\nVan Lommel provides scientific evidence that the near-death phenomenon is an authentic experience that cannot be attributed to imagination, psychosis, or oxygen deprivation. He further reveals that after such a profound experience, most patients\' personalities undergo a permanent change. In van Lommel\'s opinion, the current views on the relationship between the brain and consciousness held by most physicians, philosophers, and psychologists are too narrow for a proper understanding of the phenomenon. In Consciousness Beyond Life, van Lommel shows that our consciousness does not always coincide with brain functions and that, remarkably and significantly, consciousness can even be experienced
